1f57f 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
1f6ba Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
1f84a status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1f902 GPIB status vector:
1f917 status[0] - Device Clear State
1f936  status[1] - Device Trigger State
1f958  status[2] - Listener Active State
1f97c status[3] - Talker Active State
1f99d status[4] - Attention line asserted
1f9c2 status[5] -
1f9ce Controller In Charge
1f9e3  status[6] - Remote State
1f9fd  status[7] - Lockout State
1fa19 status[8] - I/O Completed 
1fa35 status[9] - not used
1fa4a  status[10]- not used
1fa60  status[11]- not used
1fa77 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
1fa9f status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
1fabf  status[14]- Timeout occured
1fadc  status[15]- GPIB error detected
1fb00 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
1fb35 GPIB Error:
1fb46 -No error
1fb55 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
1fb7c -No listeners detected on write
1fba1 -Controller not addressed correctly
1fbca -Invalid argument(s)
1fbe5 (perhaps bad address string????)
1fc0b -Function requires GPIB to be SC
1fc31 -I/O operation aborted
1fc4d -hardware not present
1fc68 -DMA error
1fc78 -DMA bus timeout
1fc8e -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
1fcb5 progress
1fcc3 -function not implemented
1fce2 -file system error
1fcfa -shareable board exclusively owned
1fd22 -GPIB bus error (commands)
1fd42 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
1fd5e -SRQ line cannot be cleared
1fd7f -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
1fdd9 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string.

2e015 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
2e0cd GPIB status vector:
2e0e2 status[0] - Device Clear State

2e26a status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
2e28a  status[14]- Timeout occured
2e2a7  status[15]- GPIB error detected
2e2c9 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
2e3c6 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
2e4fc The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
2e56d   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
2e59d  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
2e5cc  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device.

608c5      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

6d33d f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
6d43f      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
6d472      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
6d4a1      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
6d4db      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
6d514      error, and a positive value is a warning.
6d544      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
6d573      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
6d5a4 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
6d600 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
6d759      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
6d78d      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
6d7c7      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
6d800      error, and a positive value is a warning.
6d830      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
6d862      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

74d9a /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
74ece Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
74fe2 VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
7513b True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

77d1c Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.

7fec5 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
7ffc1 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
8011a      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
8014e      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
80188      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
801c1      error, and a positive value is a warning.

80223      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

9b001 instr vtl global
9b132 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.$

a4d30 (I32) 
a4d37 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
a4e33 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
a4f8c      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
a4fc0      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
a4ffa      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
a5033      error, and a positive value is a warning.
a5063      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
a5095      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
a50c6 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

a5160 no error

a5170 (ABC) 
a5177 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
a522e f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
a5330      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
a5363      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
a5392      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
a53cc      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
a5405      error, and a positive value is a warning.
a5435      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
a5464      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
a5495 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

a55ff (i32) The error code associated with an error.  Possible values:

bf9c3 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
bfb1c      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
bfb50      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
bfb8a      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
bfbc3      error, and a positive value is a warning.
bfbf3      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
bfc25      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
bfc56 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
bfce2 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
bfdc8 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
bfdf7 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
bfe16 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
bfe50 Optional Parameter Default Values:
bfe73     bd - GPIB board (0)
bfe8b     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
bfeb4     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
bfee1     logical addr - VXI logical address 
bff0a EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.

d3386 84(u32) task ID: identifies the group and I/O pattern.D@(u32) pattern: specifies the new state of the lines in the port.
d3401 x(i32) line mask: determines which lines in the port the write affects. If you set line mask to -1, the VI writes to the entire port and sets all the lines in the port to the states specified by the bits in pattern. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI changes only line n in the port to the state that bit n of pattern specifies. d9d05 (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

e0c99 gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
e0d01 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
e0da6 When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
e0f34 ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
e1176 (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
e1205 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
e12cd      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
e1301      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
e133b      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
e1375      error, and a positive value is a warning.
e13a5      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
e13d7      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
e1408 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
e1481 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module."
e15c9 no error
e15d2 ERROR
e15d8 no error
e15e1 ERROR
e15e8 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
e16d8 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
e1831      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
e1865      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
e189f      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
e18d9      error, and a positive value is a warning.
e1909      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
e193b      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
e196c 1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

e6bef 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

ec9f7 no error
eca00 ERROR

eca0f ERROR
eca17 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
ecac2 displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
ecb35 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
ecbbc displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
ecc58 no dialog
ecc62 OK message
ecc6d continue or stop message
ecc89 exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
ecd4d (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
ecd8c cancels error under the following conditions:
ecdbc If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
ecf10 sets error under the following conditions:
ecf3d If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
ed076 b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
ed0d8 error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
ed177 no exception
ed185 cancel error on match
ed19b set error on match
ed1af user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
ed28b user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
ed365 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
ed395 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
ed412 error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
ed49f jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
ed509 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.

ed6a5 |xerror out contains the same information as status out, code out, and source out. It has the same structure as error in.
ed721 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.

f9809 Code
f980e error codes (hidden)
f9959 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

fa1a1 GetCommErr
fa1c4 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.SD
fa470 message
fa4eb  INSTRUCTIONS:
fa4fb Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
fa7f3 Other Uses:
fa801 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
fa97d user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
faa7e exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  H

105afd  INSTRUCTIONS:
105b0d Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
105e05 Other Uses:
105e13 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
105f8f user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
106090 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
1062c7 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

10759b The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
1075f6 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
1076e0 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
107768 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.

108cff yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
108d79 &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
108e19 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
108fa2 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
10903c M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
10918d )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

10dc07 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
10dc87 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
10dd66 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.

10f332 RSRC
10f339 LVINLBVW
10f347 $yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
10f3c2 =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
10f479 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
10f602 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
10f69b J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
10f7e9 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.
